b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e \xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x93 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x87\xf0\x9d\x90\x84 \xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\x98 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91 \xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x98 \xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x93 (\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x80) \xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x87 \xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b \xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b \xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\n\n\xf0\x9d\x90\xb5\xf0\x9d\x91\xa6: \xf0\x9d\x91\x87\xe2\x84\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x92 \xf0\x9d\x91\x80\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x94\xf0\x9d\x91\x92\xf0\x9d\x91\x9a\xf0\x9d\x91\x92\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\xf0\x9d\x91\xa1\n\xf0\x9d\x91\x80\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\x90\xe2\x84\x8e 13, 2024\n\nBENECO officially inked yesterday a one year Emergency Power Supply Agreement (EPSA) with Limay Power Inc. (LPI), a subsidiary of San Miguel Global Power, that ensured the continuous supply of electricity for our member consumers in the next 12 months. The EPSA saved us from the brink of disconnection as the National Grid Corp. of the Phil. (NGCP), the country\xe2\x80\x99s transmission operator, gave notice on March 7, 2024  that BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s substations will no longer receive electricity effective 12:01 PM on March 13, 2024. That was supposed to be today. \n\nThe NGCP issued the notice as a matter of protocol after receiving word from Team Phil. Energy Corp. (TPEC) that its 20 year power supply contract with BENECO will already end on the midnight of March 12, 2024. \n   \nHonestly, we got worried a lot. Word was spreading fast that BENECO will be disconnected from the grid at 12:01 today. What could salvage the electric cooperative would be a new power supply contract or a proof that BENECO is a direct player in the Wholesale Electricity Spot Market (WESM). As of 8 AM yesterday, we did not have both. \n\nBut our prayers were answered. Around 10 AM yesterday, BENECO sat with San Miguel Global Power officials to put signatures on the dotted line. The EPSA was sent to the NGCP. In the afternoon, the transmission operator recalled the notice of disconnection. \n\nWe wish to state though that the EPSA was not a fly by night pact or one that was hurriedly and hastily executed just to stave off the threat of disconnection. The EPSA was the result of a series of negotiations with San Miguel only that the desire for its completion came just hours before disconnection. \n\nWhy EPSA? The EPSA, as per rules of the Energy Regulatory Commission (ERC), is an agreement that is brief in nature \xe2\x80\x93 one year. It is resorted to by distribution utilities as a stop gap measure while trying to secure a new power supplier that could offer a long term contract. This means that BENECO must be able to complete a Competitive Selection Process (CSP) for a new power supplier within the next 12 months. \n\nBut how come BENECO had reached this far for an EPSA? BENECO has not been remiss in its bid to secure a new power supplier in anticipation of the exit of TPEC. It started its efforts as early as 2019. But the pandemic and subsequent intervening events beyond the control of BENECO haplessly placed BENECO in an unenviable position of not being able to come to grips with a new contract. BENECO thus had no option but to go for an EPSA. \n\nWe hope that we can secure this year a new long term contract. We will do it with force and determination to slay any fear of disconnection among our member consumers. \n\nThe EPSA is half the battle won. But it gave us a breath of relief.'

b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\x87\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x92 \xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x84 \xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\n\nBENECO consumers will expect an increase in their monthly power bill this March, 2024 mainly due to an increase in the transmission charges imposed by the National Grid Corporation of the Phil. (NGCP) particular on its ancillary service charges. As per BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s computation, the increase is quite substantial, prompting BENECO to ask the NGCP the reason for the sudden surge of the ancillary service charge. \n\nIn a letter dated March 7 to NGCP\xe2\x80\x99s Ma. Cynthia Manrique, NGCP\xe2\x80\x99s revenue and regulatory affairs head, BENECO general manager Melchor Licoben sought to clarify the sudden increase in the ancillary service charge from January to February, 2024. \xe2\x80\x9cThere is a whooping increase of 509 per cent for the contingency reserve,\xe2\x80\x9d Licoben stated. This translates to a cost of P21.3 million for BENECO which is a 218 per cent increase from the previous January billing.\nNGCP is the duly franchised operator of the country\xe2\x80\x99s transmission system. It collects from distribution utilities transmission charges of which ancillary services is a component.\n\nDue to the increase, residential consumers will expect an increase of P0.3667 per kilowatt hour (kWh) in transmission charges alone. This will also mean an increase of P0.4705 per kWh for low voltage commercial industrial consumers, public buildings and streetlights. For high voltage consumers \xe2\x80\x93 like commercial and public buildings -- the increase will be P203.80 per kW.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cUpon receipt of the latest NGCP billing last March 6, we were alarmed when we saw the P21.3 million increase in the transmission billing. BENECO immediately wrote them a clarificatory letter with an earnest request that they also publish the reason for NGCP\xe2\x80\x99s almost P22 million pesos increase in transmission charges billing,\xe2\x80\x9d Olive Bete, Executive Services and Regulatory Compliance Officer (ESRCO) from the office of the General Manager, explained.\n\nFor residential consumers, they will also pay more - from P9.9796 per kWh in February to P10.4435 per kWh in March. This means an increase of P0.4369 per kWh. So, for a typical family that consumes an average of 100 kWh a month, they will have to shell out P46.39 per kWh more for the month of March, including value added tax.\nLicoben further asked NGCP to make an advisory for consumers\xe2\x80\x99 guidance which Licoben said has not been done up of this writing. The meter reading has started today and the bill the meter readers will issue to the consumers will now reflect the increase in ancillary charges. ***CJG'

Melchor Licoben, general manager, and Steve Cating, Task Force chairperson. (LSI)'

b'ADVISORY-2024-04\nUNAUTHORIZED INSTALLATION OF FACILITIES\n\nWe wish to inform the public that unauthorized installation of facilities like Closed Circuit Television (CCTV), streetlights, community speakers, electric or other utility wires, water hose, tarpaulins and the like, to BENECO poles and tapping its power supply directly to the secondary/service lines is strictly prohibited.\n\nUnauthorized installation and illegal tapping of power supply is a violation of Republic Act 7832, The Anti-Electricity and Electric Transmission Lines/Materials Pilferage Act of 1994 and BENECO Policy 6-4 which imposes penalty.\n\nBENECO reserves the right to outrightly remove such unauthorized  installation without prior notice and BENECO shall not be held responsible for any damage or loss. \n\nPlease understand that many installations / attachments on BENECO poles  affect the safety of personnel and response time especially during emergency repair and maintenance activities of electric distribution lines and equipment.\n\nIf you are operating especially a CCTV, streetlights and community speakers installed on poles outside your premises and were not covered by a contract with BENECO, kindly inform us and provide the complete inventory so we can easily conduct verification and do appropriate action. \n\nFor inquiries, you may contact us at the following: \n\n Trunk line                :   637-4400\n Cellphone numbers :  Globe \xe2\x80\x93 09175921698\n                                     Smart \xe2\x80\x93 09088657202\n\nTHE MANAGEMENT'

The electric cooperative, through James Palicdon, a BENECO community relations officer,  also took the opportunity to discuss about share capital, service connection applications and various requests like pole relocation.\n\nThe meeting went by as the mission\xe2\x80\x99s volunteers were doing services for health concerns that needed medicine and surgery. The team also provided services for dentistry, optometry, herbal medicine, nursing, adolescent health, ventosa, and other alternative medicine. \n\nThe purchase of medicine and the presence of BENECO during the medical and dental mission are part of the cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s Corporate Social Responsibility (CSR). The Aspulan\xe2\x80\x99s committee on CSR also supported the activity. The Aspulan is the duly registered labor-management-cooperation of the coop.\n\nThe 600 residents served that day received a total of at least 1400 different treatments from the team of 124 volunteer healers. ***LSI'

b'BENECO FEBRUARY POWER RATES DOWN; \nConsumers can spend more for the valentines month \nBy: Laarni S. Ilagan\n\nConsumers of the Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO) will pay less in their power bills this February.\nBENECO\'s computed February rate for residential consumers is at P9.9796/kWh, representing a decrease of P0.1455/kwh compared to January\xe2\x80\x99s rate of P10.1251/kWh.  \n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe reduction of P0.1455 per kWh will mean a  P14.55 savings for every 100 kWh electric consumption for residential consumers,\xe2\x80\x9d Ivory Paatan, BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s rates analyst, explained.\nNot only residential consumers will enjoy less power cost, BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s commercial, industrial, and public buildings (government) consumers will also pay lesser for their February billing.\n\nBENECO\xe2\x80\x99s commercial low voltage is at P9.1752/kWh from P9.3234/kWh (P0.1482/kwh decrease); commercial high voltage at P7.9652/kWh from P8.1155/kWh (P0.1503/kwh decrease); industrial rate at P9.1438/kWh from P9.2921/kWh (P0.1482/kwh decrease); public building low voltage at P9.1474/kWh from P9.2956/kWh (P0.1482/kwh decrease); and public building high voltage at P7.9374/kWh compared to January\xe2\x80\x99s rate of P8.0877/kWh (P0.1503/kwh decrease)," Paatan elaborated. \n\nThe computed across the board decrease for all consumers for February compared to last month\xe2\x80\x99s rate was attributed to the reduction of lifeline rate, senior citizen discount rate and generation system charge rate caused by pilferage recovery for January amounting to P665,072.34 from three (apprehended) accounts, Fraiser Angayen, Non-Network Services Department (NNSD) manager, explained further. \n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe unexpected decrease in rates is a pleasant surprise, given the anticipation of an increase due to the Energy Regulatory Commission\xe2\x80\x99s (ERC) directive to resume collecting the Feed-in-Tariff Allocation of P0.0364 for all electricity consumers in the country.,\xe2\x80\x9d Paatan shared.\n\nFIT-ALL is collected from all consumers of electricity nation wide by distribution utilities like BENECO. It is remitted to the National Transmission Corp. (TRANSCO) of the national government. Eligible renewable energy developers can withdraw from this fund.\nDespite the increase due to the resumption of FIT-ALL collection, BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s February rate is still lower compared to our January power rate, Angayen added. \n\nThe significant decrease in number of life line rate beneficiaries following the implementation of Republic Act 11552 also reduced the amount of lifeline rate subsidy being collected from the co-op\xe2\x80\x99s non-lifeliners. BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s Lifeline Rate beneficiaries of 80,794 in December 2023 decreased to only 861 in January 2024. \n\nThe drastic decrease of lifeliners coupled with the increased efforts of BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s anti-pilferage team in their apprehension activities that resulted to the payment of three big loaders, significantly lowered the power rates for February and gave enough cushion for the co-op\xe2\x80\x99s consumers with the collection of the FIT-ALL. \n\nBENECO\xe2\x80\x99s meter readers will start their reading meters by February 10, 2024. ***LSI'

b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e \xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x92 \xf0\x9d\x90\x85\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x91 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91 \xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x84 \xf0\x9d\x90\x83\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b \xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x93 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d-\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x8a\nBy Laarni S. Ilagan\n\nThe Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO) has raised alarm over the indiscriminate disposal of trash along the Upper Agno river upstream in Man-asok, Buguias that threatens the operation of the Benguet Electric Cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s (BENECO) 3.24 megawatt (MW) Man-asok Hydro-Electric Power Plant (MHEPP).\n\nPlastic bottles, cellophane, vegetables refuse and trimmings, clothing and pampers were found to be near the facility and BENECO fears that they will clog the weir intake and desander of the power plant during typhoon season. \n\xe2\x80\x9cClogging and siltation cause lesser water going to the intake to turn the three turbines that produce electricity, resulting to less electricity generated and a loss for the co-op, \xe2\x80\x9c said Artemio Bacoco, power generation and operations department (PGOD) manager.\n\nPGOD is the office tasked by BENECO to handle the plant\xe2\x80\x99s operations. \n\xe2\x80\x9cWe want to appeal to the residents living upstream to hopefully dispose their waste properly since they are also co-owners of our mini-hydro being member-consumer-owners (MCOs),\xe2\x80\x9d Bacoco said. \n\nThe call was made during BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s monthly employee assembly in January as Bacoco emphasized that the barangays and the municpality of Buguias are partners and recipients of benefits that can be derived from the full operation of the plant, he said. \n\nBacoco said that the PGOD workers are gathering every quarter around three cubic meters of biodegradable and non-biodegradable waste at the area. \nPGOD though has adopted measures to mitigate the concern. One is the construction of a steel mesh near the pipeline of the plant to filter any waste. Trees were also planted to prevent siltation.  The plant also has its own materials recovery facility (MRF) to house plastic water bottles and other non-biodegradable waste. \nThe generation facility also experiences water scarcity during summer when most farmers upstream pump river water from the Agno river to irrigate their farms.  This results to a low water level that can manage to run only one of the three turbines, Bacoco said.\n\nFrom June 2022 when it started its operation until December 31, 2023, the plant was able to generate a total of 9.3 million kWh of which 6.7 million kWh of power was loaded to the grid'

Ilagan\n\nBENECO is on red alert. Not that there is an incoming typhoon when all its systems must be running above par, but because it\xe2\x80\x99s the flower festival season that has added to Baguio City\xe2\x80\x99s reputation as a major tourist attraction. \n\nBENECO activated its Disaster Mitigation and Emergency Response Plan (BDMERP) last February 1, 2023 in preparation for the month-long Panagbenga activities.\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe have to ensure power supply 24/7. In case power trips, we have to make sure that we restore power as soon as possible,\xe2\x80\x9d Ramel Rifani, Network Services Department (NSD) manager, said.\nThis means BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s muscle are ready for disposal at any time \xe2\x80\x93 25 crews (composed of two linemen per crew), three hotline and heavy crews (composed of 18 linemen),  two clearing teams (15 linemen) and reliable jobbers who are stationed in all the municipalities of Benguet and ready to be dispatched for any contingency. \nOffice based engineers can also be part of the filed crew, Rifani said. \nPart of the disaster plan is the availability of materials and the fast protocol for this dispatch when needed. \nThe cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s technical department and support personnel are specifically on red-alert for the following February and March events in the city -- February 3 (Grand Opening), 13 (Chinese Spring Festival Grand Parade), 15-17 (PMA Grand Alumni Homecoming), 24-25 (Grand Street dance and Float parade) and March 3 (Closing Program and Awarding Ceremonies).\n\xe2\x80\x9cBENECO does not only go on red alert during typhoon season. Even before the creation of the BDMERP in 2018, BENECO has always been pro-active in its preparation during holidays and special occasions specially at the city of Baguio like CARAA, Christmas, Holy Week and Undas. We have our task force for these in the past,\xe2\x80\x9d Rifani recalled. **LSI'

b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c\xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x85 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x85\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x92 \xf0\x9d\x90\x83\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x9f\x90\xf0\x9d\x9f\x8e\xf0\x9d\x9f\x90\xf0\x9d\x9f\x92\n\xf0\x9d\x90\xb5\xf0\x9d\x91\xa6 \xf0\x9d\x90\xbf\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\xf0\x9d\x91\x96 \xf0\x9d\x91\x86. \xf0\x9d\x90\xbc\xf0\x9d\x91\x99\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x94\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\n\xf0\x9d\x90\xb9\xf0\x9d\x91\x92\xf0\x9d\x91\x8f\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\xa2\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\xa6 02, 2024\n\nBAGUIO CITY: The number of BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s lifeline rate subsidy beneficiaries in Baguio City and Benguet is down to 861 as of January 15, 2023, no thanks to the government\xe2\x80\x99s new law on the grant of lifeline. \n\n      The electric cooperative had 80,794 lifeline beneficiaries as of December 2023 but with the passage of RA 11552, the new lifeline law, the number had to go down since the measure redefined who should be considered as lifeliners.\n\n        The lifeline subsidy grants member consumers a discount on their monthly power bill.  \n\nUnder the old set up where the 80,974 consumers belonged, the rate of subsidy or discount was as follows - 41-45 kwh (5%); 36-40 kwh (10%); 31-35 kwh (20%); 26-30 kwh (30%); 1-25 kwh (40%);  and 20 kwh and below (50%). This is regardless if they were 4Ps beneficiarie4s or not.\n\n      This system was removed as lifeliners under RA 11552 now refer to those beneficiaries of the government\xe2\x80\x99s 4Ps (Pantawid Pamilyang Pilipino Program) as well as those who are certified by the Department of Social Welfare and Development (DSWD) as belonging to the marginalized sector.       \n\nThis means that around  80,113 lifeline consumers in the original list of BENECO were delisted as the Department of Energy (DOE) directed distribution utilities to implement the new lifeline law on January 1, 2024. \n\n     Under the DSWD\xe2\x80\x99s guidelines, the 4Ps beneficiaries and those belonging to the marginalized sector must apply before the distribution utility (DU) to be considered as lifeline consumers. The DSWD was tasked to provide the DU the list of the beneficiaries.\n\n       BENECO, being a DU, cannot therefore include the new set of lifeline beneficiaries if their names are not in the DSWD list. Even if their names are in the list if they did not file an application before the electric cooperative, they will not be automatically  considered for the subsidy or discount. \n\n     The 80,974 consumers under the old system enjoyed a total P2.8 million in discount as of December last year. They were not automatically reinstated as lifeliners since under RA 11552, they have to apply as beneficiaries of the 4Ps or certified by the DSWD as living below the poverty threshold. The 80, 974 consumers enjoyed a total P35.3 million discount for the whole year.\n\n       As of January 1, 2024, there were only 861 approved applications of which 839 were 4Ps, and 22 were non-4Ps but were certified by DSWD to belong to the marginalized sector, explained Fraiser Angayen, Non-Network Services Department (NNSD) manager.\n\n     The town of Buguias yielded the most number of approved applicants at 251; Mankayan-154; Bakun-86; La Trinidad-86; Atok-52; Kapangan-45; Baguio City-43; Tublay-38; Kibungan-29; Itogon-14; Tuba-13; Sablan-5; Kabayan-2. These were the figures before the January 15 cut off that will be updated soon, according to Angayen. \n\n     On January 17, 2024, the DSWD issued the list of delisted 4Ps beneficiaries, meaning they cannot be accepted as lifeline beneficiaries. \n\n     The DOE further directed all DUs to \xe2\x80\x9cdiscontinue the grant of the lifeline rate no later than two billing cycles from the time it received the list of delisted 4Ps beneficiaries. The DU shall inform the end-user of his/her delisting based on the latest lists of 4Ps beneficiaries received from the Department of Social Welfare and Development (DSWD).\xe2\x80\x9d\n\n     BENECO has started untagging from the subsidy list those who are no longer qualified as early as June 2023.  ***LSI'

b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\xa9\xf0\x9d\x90\xa9\xf0\x9d\x90\xab\xf0\x9d\x90\x9e\xf0\x9d\x90\xa1\xf0\x9d\x90\x9e\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7\xf0\x9d\x90\xac\xf0\x9d\x90\xa2\xf0\x9d\x90\xa8\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7 \xf0\x9d\x90\xa8\xf0\x9d\x90\x9f \xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\xa5\xf0\x9d\x90\xa5\xf0\x9d\x90\x9e\xf0\x9d\x90\xa0\xf0\x9d\x90\x9a\xf0\x9d\x90\xa5 \xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\xa8\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7\xf0\x9d\x90\x9e\xf0\x9d\x90\x9c\xf0\x9d\x90\xad\xf0\x9d\x90\xa2\xf0\x9d\x90\xa8\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7 \xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x8f, \xf0\x9d\x90\x92\xf0\x9d\x90\xb2\xf0\x9d\x90\xac\xf0\x9d\x90\xad\xf0\x9d\x90\x9e\xf0\x9d\x90\xa6 \xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\xa8\xf0\x9d\x90\xac\xf0\x9d\x90\xac \xf0\x9d\x90\x83\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x96\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d \xf0\x9d\x90\xa2\xf0\x9d\x90\xa7 \xf0\x9d\x9f\x90\xf0\x9d\x9f\x8e\xf0\x9d\x9f\x90\xf0\x9d\x9f\x91\n\xf0\x9d\x90\xb5\xf0\x9d\x91\xa6: \xf0\x9d\x90\xbf\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\xf0\x9d\x91\x96 \xf0\x9d\x91\x86. \xf0\x9d\x90\xbc\xf0\x9d\x91\x99\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x94\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\n\xf0\x9d\x90\xbd\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9b\xf0\x9d\x91\xa2\xf0\x9d\x91\x8e\xf0\x9d\x91\x9f\xf0\x9d\x91\xa6 30, 2024\n\nBAGUIO CITY: The apprehension of 283 individuals with electric meters violating the anti-pilferage law in 2023 helped improve collection efficiency and lower system loss of the Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO). The apprehension activities conducted by the Special Equipment and Metering Office (SEMO) personnel in 2023 resulted to a collection of P8.5 million unpaid arrears with surcharges, and value added tax (VAT). The P8.5 million back-billed amounts for 2023 showed a P5 million increase compared to the P3 million of 2022.\n\nThese are mostly from disconnected accounts owners apprehended due to illegally reconnecting their disconnected meters and subsequently paid the penalties and arrears, according to SEMO supervisor Engr. Mario Calatan. Compared to 2022\xe2\x80\x99s 171 total apprehension, 2023\xe2\x80\x99s 283 total apprehended accounts showed BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s SEMO apprehension team intensified their activities. The impact of these activities contributed to the lowering of the SL measured at 9.69% in 2022 to only 7.57% in 2023. Lesser (single-digit) System Loss will translate to less system loss charge that consumers of electricity will pay.\n\nBENECO\xe2\x80\x99s Network Services Department (NSD) and Legal Office are handling cases of illegal connection that were apprehended and received demand letters. They are given 3-days to settle upon receipt of the demand letter. \xe2\x80\x9cFailure to settle or at least to come to BENECO and express their willingness to pay, will signal the next step which is filing of a case against them,\xe2\x80\x9d Atty. Mylene Manogan explained.\n\nSystem loss (SL) charge or stolen electricity is the third highest bill component that all consumers  of electricity pay under the unbundled rates monthly, following Generation System Charge and the Transmission System Charge. SL represents the recovery of the cost of power lost due to Technical Losses (maintenance of distribution system) and Non-technical Losses (due to pilferage or stolen electricity.)\n\nCollection efficiency (CE) measures payments collected versus billed accounts. Both SL and CE are among the key indicators of a well-managed and efficient distribution utility. A DU with low collection efficiency will experience difficulty in meeting its financial obligations to its power supplier and other service providers whose services needs to be paid\n\nMajority of the violators opted to settle with the co-op to avoid escalation of their case to the courts, after receipt of BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s demand letter following apprehension. Direct connection, illegal transfer of kilowatt hour meter, illegal reconnection, and illegal installation of KWH meter were apprehensions by the SEMO anti-pilferage apprehension team for 2023.\n\nThe bulk of apprehended accounts that opted to settle came from disconnected meters that were endorsed for inspection to the SEMO team. Apprehended owners of illegally reconnected meters pay a penalty of minimum P2500 that may increase depending on the load and its corresponding value added tax (VAT).\n\nPersons convicted of violating Republic Act 7832 Anti-Pilferage of Electricity and Theft of Electric Transmission Lines/Materials Act of 1994 face 6 years to 12 years imprisonment or a fine of P10 to 20 thousand, and not \xe2\x80\x9cprobationable.\xe2\x80\x9d'

b'\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x8c \xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x91\xf0\x9d\x90\x86\xf0\x9d\x90\x98 \xf0\x9d\x90\x83\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x80\xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x92 \xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x94\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x8b\xf0\x9d\x90\x83\xf0\x9d\x90\x88\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x86 \xf0\x9d\x90\x93\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e \xf0\x9d\x90\x81\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x8d\xf0\x9d\x90\x84\xf0\x9d\x90\x82\xf0\x9d\x90\x8e\n\nTeam Energy has recently signed the Deed of Donation that formalized the turnover of P10 million to BENECO that was used for the construction of the first phase of the electric cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s training center at barangay Alapang, La Trinidad. \nThe donation was used to complete the foundation and first floor structure of a two storey building meant to serve as a training institution.\nThe deed of donation dated January 22, 2024  said that building which will serve as an \xe2\x80\x9ceducational institution building with training and lodging facilities for the main purpose of conducting technical and non-technical training activities for BENECO employees and from those other cooperatives in the Cordillera region and other parts of the country.\xe2\x80\x9d\nTeam Energy is BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s power supplier and the donation was coursed through its social development arm, Team Energy Foundation, Inc. (TEFI).\nAsking Team Energy for a donation started during the time of the late GM Gerardo Verzosa n a bid to give chance for Benguet\xe2\x80\x99s young people who are financially challenged and whose parents cannot afford to send them to college. \n The BENECO Board of Directors (BOD) approved the Memorandum of Agreement  (MOA) with Team Energy for the donation  in May 2018.\nThe construction for Phase I (structural and roofing) of the building started in July, 2022 through Arch. Elvis Palicdon who turned over the structure to Team Energy in June, 2023. \nBENECO needs P13 million more to complete the second phase of the building that includes finishing works.  \nThe TEFI said that it granted BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s request to fund the building in recognition of the electric cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s \xe2\x80\x9ctreasure trove of experience and practice in the sustainable operations of a distribution utility(DU)  that it would like to share with neighboring DUs and others in the other regions of the country as well, their (BENECO) sustainable practices through classroom-type training and education\xe2\x80\x9d. \nMitsuhiro Kojima of TEFI and Steve Cating, chairperson of the BENECO Task Force, signed the deed of donation.\nThe building followed the establishment of the BENECO Skills Development Training Center (BSDTC) at Abatan, Buguias which is a TESDA accredited technical vocational school.\nThe school offers linemen training certification and other skills training courses such as welding, electrical installation maintenance and massage therapy. \n\xe2\x80\x9cWorking hard to realize his dream for BENECO, the late GM Verzosa exhausted all avenues looking for funding that will not burden the consumers. Coupled with his genius in financial engineering, he tirelessly requested the top leaders of TEAM Energy for the donation, recalled Engr. Jo Calawen, a member of the committee formed to work on the training center. \n-30-'

b'ADVISORY-2024-02\n \nAdvisory on Electrocution\n\nDEATH or INJURY can occur when in contact with electric power lines. BENECO has again recorded cases of electrocution incidents involving  individuals or a group working near electric power lines. Based on our records, electrocution happened mostly but not limited to the following: \n\n-On CONSTRUCTION sites when a metal or other conductive material a construction worker was holding got in contact with the electric power lines.\n\n-Other public utility or their outsourced personnel laying-out their telecommunication/cable lines and/or installing metal poles or other  conductive materials under or near the electric power lines.\n\n-Transporting machineries or equipment with high vertical reach and got in contact with telecommunication/cable lines and/or electric lines and when a person tried to free the lines for the vehicle to pass.\n\n-Other activities near power lines involving a moving equipment or any conductive materials that have touched the power lines.\n\nWe wish to advise the public to always contact and coordinate with BENECO for assistance when working near the power lines to ensure safety of life and property. ALWAYS CONSIDER ELECTRIC POWER LINES ENERGIZED.\n\nWe can be reached at the following 24/7 hotline numbers: \n Telephone number : (074) 637- 4400\n Cell phone numbers : Smart \xe2\x80\x93 09088657202\n                   Globe \xe2\x80\x93 09175921698\nFor everyone\xe2\x80\x99s information and guidance.\n\nApproved for posting :\nNSD Manager'

b'ADVISORY-2024-01\nTripartite Advisory on Lifeline IRR\n\nWe wish to inform our member consumer owners (MCOs) that a Tripartite Advisory on Lifeline IRR was issued by the Energy Regulatory Commission (ERC), the Department of Energy (DOE), and the Department of Social Welfare and Development (DSWD) on December 29, 2023.\n\nRelative thereto, effective this January 2024 billing cycle, only those qualified marginalized end-users (QMEs) who have registered and whose applications were approved from July 1, 2023 onwards will be entitled to avail of the subsidy. \n\nThus, we wish to advise all MCOs that we will now remove the lifeline rate   discount for those who are not qualified to avail as provided in the Lifeline IRR. \n\nWe strongly encourage all qualified marginalized end-users to submit their applications to avail of the discount.\n\nFor everyone\xe2\x80\x99s information and guidance.\n\nThank you.\n\nNNSD  Manager \n\nPlease follow the link for the steps on how to apply for lifeline rate discount: \n\nhttps://m.facebook.com/story.php?story_fbid=pfbid02iZGJgoTTDFs6VfL1Ykb9UuVaaokfuutbqh64v1jPsTgeoSFFc5orbw8j7oj5kp3l&id=100070933082241&mibextid=Nif5oz'

b'ADVISORY-2023-38\n\nDistribution of 2024 BENECO Calendars\n\nWe wish to inform all our member consumer owners (MCOs) that the mechanics for the distribution of calendars has been updated as follows:\n\n1. The MCOs must present their proof of payment (Official Receipt) for their December bill to the security guard assigned in the collection centers to be entitled to a calendar. \n\n2. Those who paid their bills thru banks and online payment platforms may also claim their calendar provided they present a copy of their proof of payment/s and December electricity bills.\n\n3. Each MCO will be entitled to 1 (one) calendar only. But for MCOs with multiple accounts, they will be entitled to a maximum of two (2) calendars only regardless of the number of  accounts registered in their name.\n\n4.The distribution of calendars will be on a first come, first serve basis. \n\nYou may claim the calendars from the following collection centers:\n1. Maharlika Livelihood Complex\n2. Bonuan Condominium, Happy Glenn Loop\n3. BENECO Headquarters, South Drive\n4. KM4 La Trinidad\n5. Bekkes, Buyacaoan, Buguias\n6. b'ADVISORY-2023-34\n\nREDUCTION OF SURCHARGES AND MASSIVE IMPLEMENTATION OF DISCONNECTION OF  DELINQUENT ACCOUNTS\n\nWe advise all our member consumer owners (MCOs) that due to the increasing number of delinquent accounts, the cooperative will be implementing a massive and intensified disconnection of all delinquent accounts, or those accounts with arrearages. Hence, we encourage all MCOs to pay their arrears as soon as possible to avoid disconnection.\n\nFurther, in the spirit of the upcoming yuletide season and as part of the 50th year anniversary celebration of the cooperative, please be informed that for the period December 1\xe2\x80\x9430, 2023, the cooperative will be reducing the surcharges on arrearages that will be paid during this period by 50%. Thus, we encourage all MCOs with arrearages to avail of this reduction on surcharges.   \n\nFor everyone\xe2\x80\x99s information and guidance. \n\nFRAISER P. ANGAYEN \nNNSD Manager'

b'ADVISORY-2023-36\n\nDistribution of 2024 BENECO Calendars\n\nWe wish to inform all our member consumer owners (MCOs) that the distribution of the 2024 BENECO Calendars will start on December 11, 2023. In relation, the following mechanics will be followed:\n\n1. The MCOs must present their proof of payment (Official Receipt) for their December bill to the security guard assigned in the collection centers to be entitled to a calendar.\n\n2. Each MCO will be entitled to 1 (one) calendar only. But for MCOs with multiple accounts, they will be entitled to a maximum of two (2) calendars only regardless of the number of accounts registered in their name.\n\n3. The distribution of calendars will be on a first come, first serve basis. \n\nYou may claim the calendars from the following collection centers:\n\nCollection Centers\n\n1. Maharlika Livelihood Complex\n2. Bonuan Condominium, Happy Glenn Loop\n3. BENECO Headquarters, South Drive\n4. KM4 La Trinidad\n5. Bekkes, Buyacaoan, Buguias\n6. Accredited Collecting Agents\n\nFor any concerns and inquiries you may reach us through our 24/7 contact center.\nFor everyone\xe2\x80\x99s information and guidance. \n\nFRAISER P. b'Musicians For Hope.\n\nFive young musicians with a mission brought Christmas Cheers to BENECO employees at lunch today, singing for 20 minutes tunes of yuletide joy and Hope. The choir members are Mary Daniela Rosel,17 (Guitarist), Allyssandra Eneria, 24  (Violinist), Aaron Justo, 17 (Beatboxer) Bea Orille ,20 and Judith Sang-il, 24 (Vocalist). They are members of the Pinoy Young Musicians (PYM) who showcase their  talents in mini concerts. \n\nThe young musicians are part of the group PYM-North Central Luzon who perform in various restaurants, hotels and office to support their advocacy of teaching and sharing  their talents to out of school youth like themselves.\n\nThey Conduct free lessons as well as provide free musical instruments to their peers.\n\nThrough music, the group hopes to give alternative productive activities and chance to discover talents of young people who for reasons beyond their financial capabilities  cannot continue their formal education.\n\nToday, BENECO became one of these youth\xe2\x80\x99s instrument of hope. ***LSI'

b'BENECO PRESS RELEASE\nLICOBEN IS BENECO GM! \n\nBAGUIO CITY: Engr. Melchor S. Licoben gets appointment as Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO) general manager (GM) from BENECO Task Force Interim Board of Directors following recommendation from the National Electrification Administration (NEA).\n\xe2\x80\x9cThere was no other candidate, he was the number one choice as recommended by the NEA,\xe2\x80\x9d Steve Cating, Interim BOD chairperson said speaking for the task force composed of representatives from various sectors in Baguio City and Benguet province. \n\n\xe2\x80\x9cCongratulations Engr. Melchor S. Licoben for his official appointment as GM of the Benguet Electric Cooperative going forward. We are very proud to appoint him, and there is no question of his competence as a manager and as a resource person for BENECO going forward. We look forward to growing BENECO for the next 50 years as we renew our franchise. \n\nThis endorsement of employees was further bolstered by all the local government units of Baguio city and Benguet, as well as the member-consumer-owners (MCOs) who have shown their unshakeable support. \n\nEarlier, NEA Adminsitrator Antonio Almeda promised the appointment of a GM  during the October 6 BENECO Employees Awarding and 50th Anniversary program as one of the guests of honor. \n\n\xe2\x80\x9cWe are very blessed that our prayers were granted. The struggle was all worth it. We learned important lessons, and all the hardships we have gone thru further strengthened the bond and unity of all employees,\xe2\x80\x9d Jefferd Monang said. Monang is the BENECO Labor Union president. ***LSI'

b'ADVISORY-2023-32\n\nApplication for Lifeline Rate Discount\n\nWe wish to inform our member consumer owners (MCOs) that we are now accepting applications for Lifeline Rate Discount based on the Implementing Rules and Regulations (IRR) of RA 1152, entitled \xe2\x80\x9cAn Act Extending and Enhancing the Implementation of the Lifeline Rate, Amending for the Purpose, Section 73 of RA 9136\xe2\x80\x9d and the Tripartite Advisory on the same IRR as issued by the Energy Regulatory Commission (ERC), Department of Energy (DOE), and Department of Social  Welfare and Development (DSWD). \n\nBased on Rule 6, Section 1 of the Lifeline IRR, the following are the qualified marginalized end-users who may avail of the discount:\n\nA. Qualified household-beneficiary under the Republic Act No. 11310, otherwise known as the \xe2\x80\x9cPantawid Pamilyang Pilipino Program\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9c4Ps Act\xe2\x80\x9d;\n\nB. Marginalized end-user, living below the property threshold established by the Philippine Statistics Authority (PSA), who possesses the qualification and none of the disqualifications under the Act and its IRR.\n\nAll qualified applicants may now process their applications and submit the following requirements thru our Consumer Welfare Desks located at South Drive, Baguio City or Buyacaoan, Buguias:\n\n4Ps Beneficiary:\n\ni. A Duly Accomplished Application Form;\nii. Most recent electricity bill of the electric service being applied for; and\niii. Any valid government-issued ID  containing the signature and address of the consumer\n\nOther marginalized end-users who are not 4Ps beneficiaries:\n\ni. A certification form the local SWDO issued within six (6) months prior to the filing of application, showing that his or her family  income is below the poverty threshold applicable at the time of his or her application;\nii. Most recent electricity bill of the electric service being applied for; and\niii. Any valid government-issued ID containing the signature and address of the consumer\n\nOther supporting documents:\nA. Proof of residence if electric service is not registered under the name of the applicant (barangay certification)\nB. Letter of authority if filed thru a representative and the valid government issued ID of the representative \n\nAll qualified MCOs are encouraged to apply for the Lifeline Rate Discount.\nFor everyone\xe2\x80\x99s information and guidance.\n\nThank you.\n\nFRAISER P. ANGAYEN\nDepartment Manager, NNSD'

b'JOINT CEREMONIAL ENERGIZATION AND SWITCH-ON\n\nKAYAPA, BAKUN, BENGUET: In time for BENECO\'s celebration of its 50th Founding Anniversary, BENECO celebrates with the Member-Consumer-Owners (MCOs) at Kayapa, Bakun, Benguet today. \n\nBeneficiaries from the nine (9) Sitios of Kayapa, Bakun and two (2) Sitios of Tacadang, Kibungan, Benguet, led the joint ceremonial energization and switch-on program for Sitios Lipay, Labour, Sumap, Lipucan, Bilig, Lebba, Kiwet, Upper Teg-li and Lower Biling for Kayapa, Bakun. Kibungan Mayor Cesar Molitas and members of the Municipal Council of Kibungan represented the beneficiaries of Sitios Lanipew and Asug, Tacadang, Kibungan, Benguet.\n\nIn Kayapa, P5,499,647.80 funded the erection of 73 poles, 2.5 kilometers of power lines for 1-phase primary lines and 1.4 kilometers secondary lines. While PP1,991,228,47 funded the erection of 27 posts, 1.5 kilometers primary power lines, 1.4 secondary lines. These sitios were among the last of the 2020 Sitio Electrification Program (SEP) funding granted to BENECO for sitios to be energized.\n\nHost barangay PB Mateo T. Langpaoen, expressed his gratitude in behalf of his constituents. In their desire to finally have power, Langpaoen recalled that the beneficiaries themselves helped carry the posts from the nearest road to their sitios "Umili ti nag bunbunag poste" Langpaoen said in Kankanaey.\n\nEngr. Mario Calatan, representing the Network Services Department (NSD), said the terrain proved very challenging for the BENECO Team who erected the poles and strung the power lines along the towering mountains of Kayapa, Bakun. The residents of the sitios thought having power was just a dream. \n\n"Tagtagainepen mi laeng nga mailman kami kuryente idi. Idi khan addan naiyeg nga posposte. Inikkan nakami pay ti libre nga metro. Isu nga agyaman kami la unay BENECO ti panangiyeg yu iti kuryente mi." Lecino Dalupang Daniel, 72, with six children resident beneficiary of sitio Lipay, Kayapa, Bakun, Benguet gave the response representing the beneficiaries.\n\n- LSI'
b'OUTREACH AND SWITCH-ON.\n\nOfficers and employees of BENECO, headed by Chairperson Steve Cating, visit Barangay Kayapa of Bakun, Benguet for the ceremonial switch-on of sitios energized in Bakun and Tacadang under the Sitio Electrification Program (SEP) funded by the government thru the National Electrification Administration (NEA). The program was attended by the beneficiaries of the SEP from Bakun and Kibungan including the barangay officials and LGU officials from both municipalities.\n\nSimultaneously, an outreach program was also conducted in coordination with Baguio Lions Everlasting bringing free medical services to the constituents of Kayapa.\n\nThe activity was also attended by representatives of NEA who conducted the line inspection of the accomplished projects for acceptance.\n\nPhotos: LSI'

b'PRESS RELEASE\nJune 08, 2023\n\nTRANSFORMER NOW BEING TRANSPORTED TO BENECO\n\nSanto Domingo, Ilocos Sur: The 10 MVA substation transformer to be leased by the Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO) from the Ilocos Sur Electric Cooperative (ISECO) is now being transported to Mankayan, Benguet. \n\nAs of press time, the transformer just left Santo Domingo. Engineers from the Benguet Electric Cooperative (BENECO) closely coordinated with personnel of the Ilocos Sur Electric Cooperative (ISECO) for the transport of the transformer. The 10 MVA transformer from ISECO will temporarily replace the 3.75 MVA damaged transformer of BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s substation at Bulalacao, Mankayan, Benguet while the cooperative looks for a new transformer. \n\nThe long period to acquire a new transformer compelled BENECO to look for a transformer to be leased in the meantime. The new transformer to be purchased must be customized to BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s specifications and will have to undergo the tedious process of bidding. Joaquin Calawen and Christopher Tait, BENECO engineers, are leading the BENECO contingent ferrying the leased transformer from ISECO to Mankayan via the Halsema highway. \n\nThe ISECO transformer\xe2\x80\x99s oil has been drained and its cooling fins and bushing were detached in the meantime to ensure an easier and safer transport along Nagulian Road up to Halsema highway. Artemio Bacoco, acting general manager, is again appealing for the patience and understanding of the affected consumers in Mankayan and some parts of Buguias town who continue to have no light as of this writing.***LSI'

b'PRESS RELEASE\nJune 07, 2023\n\nABATAN, BUGUIAS: Two teams composed of 15 linemen worked fast to finish the diversion of some communal transformers from Circuit 4 to Sinipsip Substation (Circuit 6) to restore power to parts of Buyacaoan and Abatan, Buguias, yesterday.\n\nThe team is led by Construction and Maintenance Officer Engr. Roy Olatic. Circuit 4 is part of the affected areas by the typhoon Betty-damaged Bulalacao, Mankayan Substation that rendered the town of Mankayan and parts of Buguias without power.\n\nPraying for continuing good weather, Network Services Department (NSD) OIC department manager Engr. Mario Calatan said that BENECO will be able to already restore electricity in these two areas where the Northern Benguet District Hospital and the Municipal Hall are located.\n\nThe Bulalacao Substation serves Circuit 5 (Mankayan) and Circuit 4 (Buguias). The damage to the Bulalacao Substation raised the cost of Typhoon Betty\xe2\x80\x99s damages suffered by BENECO to more than P5.8 million as of June 5, 2023.\n\nBENECO earlier assured the MCOs in the area that as long as the weather is under normal conditions during the transport to its testing and commissioning of the Bulalacao substation transformer replacement, the expected restoration of power will be by June 15, 2023.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe ISECO Board during their meeting approved the request of BENECO for the rental of the 10 MVA power transformer. BENECO has mobilized their equipment to haul the transformer from ISECO to Mankayan and is expected to arrive soon. It will take BENECO five days  to install and commission the transformer upon delivery, however it will depend on the weather condition,\xe2\x80\x9d Engr. Artemio Bacoco, Acting General Manager said.\n\n\xe2\x80\x9cIf all the testing and commissioning is successful then the transformer  will be energized. Hence, the power supplying  the two municipalities  including some parts of Cervantes will be completely energized,\xe2\x80\x9d Bacoco explained further.***LSI'

(ISECO) Board of Directors who will be discussing our request in their Board Meeting  today, June 5, 2023.\n\nWe understand the difficulty and hassle of having no electricity on demand, and we beg for further understanding and patience, but there are processes and   procedures that we have to prepare and follow, as this is a major undertaking by your cooperative.\n\nISECO Management has prepared the MOA with BENECO in anticipation of their Board of Director\xe2\x80\x99s approval today. \n\nUpon securing ISECO Board\xe2\x80\x99s approval, mobilization of our trucking partner commences immediately tomorrow (June 6, 2023) to bring the power transformer from ISECO to our Bulalacao, Mankayan Substation for installation, testing, and other works needed in preparation for the immediate energization and  normalization of service.\n\nAgain, your Cooperative would like to express its sincerest gratitude for your  patience and understanding.\n\nENGR. Ramel Rifani, BENECO Acting General Manager, said of the cooperative\xe2\x80\x99s preparedness a day prior the super typhoon\xe2\x80\x99s expected landfall in the country.\nThe co-op has started to ensure sufficient inventory of materials: poles, transformers, and line hardware in preparation for the damages that super typhoon Mawar will incur, Rifani said.\nAs of Friday afternoon, the NSD has prepared the usual notice for personnel and jobbers in readiness for the declaration of red alert and the corresponding mobilization of personnel when the need arises through its Task force, Rifani said.\n\xe2\x80\x9cThe activation of BENECO\xe2\x80\x99s disaster preparedness bible\xe2\x80\x94the BENECO Disaster Mitigating and Emergency Restoration Plan (BDMERP) that has been in place for several years--will depend on the damages incurred and the scope of areas with power interruption, even if there is no storm signal,\xe2\x80\x9d Rifani explained.\nIf the Office of the Civil Defense (OCD) in the region declares a red alert, BENECO will also automatically activate its Task Force and its BDMERP.\nThe Commander on the Ground will be Engr. Mario Calatan, NSD\xe2\x80\x99s OIC-Department Manager.\n \xe2\x80\x9cBENECO as a world class utility company has been following its protocol, and is prepared for this kind of contingencies. We can ramp up the team once there is need for it,\xe2\x80\x9d Interim Board Chairperson Steve Cating said, expressing his confidence to BENECO disaster preparedness team.\nCating called for patience and understanding once the typhoon hits Baguio and Benguet and consumers will experience power blackout, since time is needed for the BENECO linemen to safely restore power.***LSI'
